## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration depends on position, velocity, and possibly time. The equation of motion generalizes the simple harmonic oscillator with nonlinear restoring forces, damping, and/or external driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Van der Pol type: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with drive)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (Mathieu-type parametric excitation)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (position-dependent stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Cubic damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v**3 + c2 * v (cubic velocity-dependent damping)
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric restoring force)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (quadratic nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillator symmetry
- Even-power restoring terms (x²) → asymmetric potential wells indicating broken symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v → linear energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Products of position powers and velocity (x²*v) → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillators
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → external periodic driving force causing resonance phenomena
- Position multiplied by periodic time function x*cos(c*t) → parametric excitation leading to parametric resonance
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system where phase portrait fully characterizes dynamics
- Rational functions of position x/(1+c*x²) → bounded restoring force modeling saturable nonlinearity
- Sign-preserving nonlinear velocity terms v*abs(v) or v³ → nonlinear drag forces (aerodynamic or fluid resistance)

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*sin(x)*v - c1*beta*v
Candidate formulas: 51

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0313132*v**3 - 0.657729*v*sin(x) - 1.31546*v + 0.383671*sin(t)`

The key terms are:
1. `sin(t)` term
2. `v` term (linear in v)
3. `v**3` term
4. `v*sin(x)` term — this is the critical term to match

The challenge is matching `v*sin(x)`. Let me check if any candidate can produce `v*sin(x)` through its terms.

**sin(x) as a Taylor series:** sin(x) = x - x³/3! + x⁵/5! - x⁷/7! + ...

So `v*sin(x) = v*x - v*x³/6 + v*x⁵/120 - ...`

This is an infinite series, so polynomial approximations with finite terms (like candidates 8, 9, 10, 15, etc.) cannot match exactly.

**Candidates with `v*exp(c*x²)` or `v*exp(c*x)` type terms:** These generate exponential functions, not sin(x), so they can't match sin(x) either.

**Candidates with `v*log(c*x² + 1)`:** This is logarithmic, not sin(x).

**Candidates with `v*x**c` (power law):** Setting c to any value gives a monomial, not sin(x).

**Candidates with `v/x**(1/3)`:** This is another monomial.

**Candidates with `v*x*exp(c*x)`:** This is x times an exponential, not sin(x).

**Key insight:** None of the candidate formulas contain a `sin(x)` term or any combination of finite elementary functions that can exactly reproduce `sin(x)` for all x.

Let me verify: The GT requires `v*sin(x)` as a function of x. For a candidate to match, it needs to produce `sin(x)` multiplied by `v` using its available terms. 

- Polynomial terms in x (finite number) cannot equal sin(x) for all x.
- Exponential terms like `exp(c*x)` or `exp(c*x²)` cannot equal sin(x).
- `x**c` (power terms) cannot equal sin(x).
- `log(c*x² + 1)` cannot equal sin(x).
- `|v|` terms don't help with the x-dependence.

**For `cos(c*t + c)` vs `sin(t)`:** Note that `cos(c₃*t + c₄)` with c₃=1, c₄=-π/2 gives `cos(t - π/2) = sin(t)`. Similarly `sin(c₁ + c₂*t)` can match. So the `sin(t)` part is fine.

**The v³ term** is present in most candidates. ✓

**The linear v term** is present in most candidates. ✓

**The v*sin(x) term** — this is the bottleneck. No candidate has `v*sin(x)` or any mechanism to produce it exactly.

Going through all 51 candidates systematically, none of them contain `sin(x)` as a building block (they all use polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, or power laws in x). Since `sin(x)` cannot be expressed as a finite combination of these elementary functions for all x, none of the candidates can match the GT.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: -0.0313*v³ - 0.6577*v*sin(x) - 1.3155*v + 0.3837*sin(t)**

The key terms are:
1. `sin(t)` — a sinusoidal term in t
2. `v` — linear in v
3. `v*sin(x)` — v times sin(x)
4. `v³` — cubic in v

The critical challenge is the `v*sin(x)` term. None of the candidates explicitly contain `sin(x)`, so I need to check if any combination of basis functions in x can exactly reproduce `sin(x)` for all x in the domain.

**Key observation:** `sin(x)` is a transcendental function. It cannot be exactly represented by:
- Polynomials in x (x, x², x³, x⁴, x⁵...)
- Exponentials (exp(cx), exp(cx²))
- Powers (x^c, x^(1/3))
- Logarithms (log(cx²+1))
- Rational functions (x/(cx²+1))
- Products like x*exp(cx), x²*exp(cx), x³*exp(cx)

None of these are equivalent to sin(x). The Taylor series of sin(x) = x - x³/3! + x⁵/5! - ... has infinitely many terms, so no finite polynomial can match it exactly. Similarly, exponentials, logarithms, and power functions are linearly independent from sin(x).

Let me verify: every candidate multiplies v by functions of x that are combinations of polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, or power functions. None include `sin(x)` as a basis function multiplied by v.

The GT requires a `v*sin(x)` term with a non-zero coefficient (-0.6577). Since sin(x) cannot be exactly represented by any finite combination of the basis functions available in any candidate, **no candidate can match the GT**.

Let me also check the `sin(t)` / `cos(t)` part: Many candidates have `cos(c3*t + c4)` or `sin(c1 + c2*t)`, which can match `sin(t)` by setting appropriate phase shifts and frequencies. That part is fine.

The `v` and `v³` terms are present in most candidates. That's also fine.

The fundamental problem remains: **none of the candidates contain `v*sin(x)`**, and no combination of the offered basis functions (polynomials, exponentials, logs, powers of x) can exactly equal `sin(x)`.
